## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This is a chemical reaction kinetics problem where dA/dt represents the rate of change of concentration A. The rate law typically depends on concentration A raised to some power (reaction order), and time t may appear explicitly if the rate constant is time-dependent or through complex mechanistic pathways.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law dependence on concentration)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with back reaction from constant product)
- Autocatalytic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with finite reagent)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (self-inhibition or substrate inhibition)
- Second-order with two species: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (pseudo-second-order with stoichiometric constraint)
- Time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (exponentially varying rate constant)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline)
- Parallel reaction pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous reaction channels)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or heterogeneous kinetics)
- Quadratic polynomial in A: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (general second-order expansion of rate law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple integer reaction order → dA/dt as a monomial in A: c*A^n with n = 0, 1, 2, 3
- Reversible reactions → rate law with both positive and negative terms in concentration: c0*A + c1*(c2 - A)
- Autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics → quadratic terms A*(c - A) producing sigmoidal concentration profiles
- Diffusion-limited reactions in heterogeneous systems → fractional powers of concentration A^(1/2), A^(2/3)
- Competing parallel pathways → sum of power-law terms with different exponents: c0*A^n1 + c1*A^n2
- Enzyme-like saturation in concentration dependence → rational functions A/(A + c) indicating mechanistic saturation
- Time-dependent rate constants from photochemistry or temperature ramps → explicit multiplicative time factors like t^c or exp(c*t)
- Conservation laws coupling multiple species → rate expressed as polynomial in single concentration via stoichiometric substitution
